Letter 220

Dear Sirs, I recently read the news column of your newspaper on the 19th, which contained the "Cao Zhenhai Arson Sentence" news, which said, "Cao Zhenhai rented a Linhua Yanzhi Store at No. 603, Ronghuali, Malang Road, from Ningbo native Lin Rongbao in February last year. The business was still quite developed. In February this year, Lin Rongbao and his partners Wang Guanglan and apprentice Jiang Ruixing were dug away. They jointly invested with Wang Guanglian, a native of Zhenjiang, at the entrance of Laohuali, which is connected to Cao's store, to open a Ronghua store," etc. After checking, the house at No. 603 Malang Road was ordered by me, and the Linhua store was also created by me. Last year, I changed to another industry and had no intention of operating it, so I rented it to Cao Zhenhai for business. As for the Ronghua store at No. 605, it was created by Wang Guanglian's sole investment, and the house was leased directly from Yihe Company, which has nothing to do with me. Moreover, the name Wang Guanglan mentioned in your newspaper cannot be found at all. The contents of your newspaper are thought to be mistaken by hearsay. Please correct it in particular to clarify the truth. I am grateful to the editor of Shenbao for his peace. Lin Yongbao respectfully, October 20th,

Dear Editor, Yesterday your newspaper published a news item "Dazhonghua Rubber Factory Resumes Work Well Yesterday," which said that labor and capital have now agreed on conditions, etc., which is not true. After investigation, the workers went to resume work yesterday, and obtained the permission of our association in advance. As for the words signed by the factory's coercion, it is close to the nature of employment and is unethical. How can the labor-capital conditions be confused? According to the labor-capital conditions, it must be signed by the two main bodies (the labor union is the labor party) to be legal. How can each worker sign it alone? The Industrial Communications Agency has abandoned its objective responsibility, which is a strange thing. The matter concerns the social hearing and the great affairs of our association. Please publish it in the letter column according to the situation to correct it. May the matter be in order and I wish you a safe writing. Shanghai Second District Rubber Industry Trade Union.

Kidnappers Send Letters Extorting Huge Sums of Money, Small Hostages Found in Apartments 221

Kidnapping Case in Huajie Solved in French Concession

Five Male and Female Kidnappers Arrested in Succession

Yu Sanfu, a Mi Po native, is 40 years old. His wife, Ms. Zhang, is the same age as Yu and lives at No. 50, Hongchenfang, Oujia Road, under the jurisdiction of the Public Security Bureau of the Fifth District of Zhabei. They have a son named Changgeng, who is four years old this year. Yu runs a coppersmith's workshop and his business is quite developed, and he has assets, which has aroused the envy of bandits. At about 3:00 pm on the 2nd of this month, Yu's son, Changgeng, was led by a wet nurse to play at the entrance of the alley. Suddenly, several kidnappers came and kidnapped the child Yu Changgeng. At that time, Yu reported to the police agencies in the Chinese Concession, requesting investigation. After three or four days, Yu received a letter from the bandits, extorting a ransom of 50,000 yuan. Because the negotiations were not settled, the child is still not out of danger. Until 10:00 am yesterday, the special agency of the French Concession Detective Superintendent Jin Jiulin learned that a gang of kidnappers was hiding in Room 18, Central Apartment, No. 40, Daodeli, Beile Road, in the French Concession, waiting for the person in charge to send someone to negotiate. Superintendent Jin then led Detectives Zhang Ziying, Qin Youyu, Wang Ronggui, Bao Tan Tian Shiqing, Jin Bingwen, Tao Ronglin, Xu Guilin, etc., and went to Room 18 of the Central Apartment without making a sound, and arrested two kidnappers, Hua Zhongbiao from Shaoxing (43 years old) and Qian Jintu (32 years old). They confessed that the location of the hidden ticket agency was in the pavilion on the second floor of No. 5, Hongshoufang, Busa Boma White Road, in the British Concession. The detectives immediately met with the Chinese and foreign detectives sent by the Public Concession to go there, and rescued the small hostage Yu Changgeng, and arrested the male and female bandits watching the ticket, Zhang Taixing (38 years old), Zhang Zufat (31 years old), and Zhang Shangshi (19 years old, Zufat's wife) from Shaoxing. Then, at Room 432, Dashanghai Hotel, No. 423, Tianjin Road, they continued to capture three bandits, Zhuang Qian (28 years old), Wang Zhencheng (38 years old), and Huang Youmei (all three from Shaoxing), and the detectives took them back to the French Concession together, and notified the person in charge, and first took the hostage back. The bandits were ordered to be detained separately by the Western Detectives, pending interrogation. The Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau was also informed that the hostage's residence and the kidnapping location were in Zhabei in Huajie, so the Detective Team sent detectives to the French Concession to request the extradition of the bandits to be interrogated.

X X X X

Page 15

Kaiming Edition of the Twenty-Five Histories Special Issue

The Compilation of the Twenty-Five Histories: The Twenty-Four Histories and the New History of Yuan 222

— Zhou Yutong

Before an ideal general history appears, the Twenty-Four Histories have their own value of existence. The Twenty-Four Histories are so vast in scope, and the organization is certainly not perfect, but there is no way, if we want to know a little more about history, we always have to consult them. We cannot use our current perspective to blame the people who compiled history in the past, saying that they only knew how to stick to the methods of Sima Qian and Ban Gu, and compile dynastic histories like drawing a gourd, because in a feudal society, only such histories are suitable products.

On the other hand, the Twenty-Four Histories have indeed become a complete system, not a meaningless compilation. Although it is in the biographical style, most of them have "Zhi" and "Biao," etc. The parts missing from each history have been supplemented and revised by scholars of past dynasties, and they are almost complete. Taking the Twenty-Four Histories as the backbone and adding the supplements is a very rich cultural history. Furthermore, there are overlapping parts in the Twenty-Four Histories, the most obvious of which are the History of the Five Dynasties and the New History of the Five Dynasties, the History of Tang and the New History of Tang. This repetition is not just to boast of abundance. Generally, the new intention lies in correction, and with the new, abandoning the old will also lose the benefit of reference and mutual evidence, so concurrent collection and juxtaposition have their own meaning.

The compilation of the History of Yuan in the Ming Dynasty was very sloppy. The people who participated in it at that time did not know Mongolian, and they did not know much about the institutions and culture of the Yuan Dynasty. They just copied it randomly, which led to many errors. General criticism says that the History of Yuan is the most desolate among the histories, which aroused the motivation of a group of scholars to study or transform the History of Yuan. Those who studied the History of Yuan include Qian Daxin, Li Wentian, Hong Jun, Ding Qian, Zhang Xiangwen, etc. Their works have revised the History of Yuan, but only in part. Those who intended to transform the History of Yuan include Shao Yuanping, Wei Yuan, Tu Ji, etc. Tu Ji's History of the Mongols was published, but it was not completed. Shao Yuanping's Yuan History Compilation and Wei Yuan's New History of Yuan are just "chronicle" work, at most equivalent to Wang Hongxu's Draft History of Ming. Ke Shaomin's New History of Yuan was completed last. This book is meticulously sourced and rigorously established, which is the opposite of the hasty completion of the History of Yuan. Although Chen Yuan criticized that it is better to annotate and supplement the History of Yuan than to transform it, like Pei Songzhi's annotation of the Records of the Three Kingdoms and Chu Shaosun's supplement to the Records of the Historian, this is actually the meaning of "blaming the worthy." Compared with the New History of the Five Dynasties and the New History of Tang, this book is more than just "no shame." Kaiming Bookstore includes it in the system of the Twenty-Four Histories and combines it into the Twenty-Five Histories, which can be said to be undoubtedly appropriate.

The Twenty-Five Histories and National Rejuvenation 223

— Pan Zhizhan

Those who do not read the history of their own country cannot spontaneously generate patriotism, and those who do not understand the past of the development of their own nation cannot be expected to shoulder the responsibility of rejuvenating the nation. It is a pity that our country's historical records are too numerous to be counted, and scholars often suffer from the difficulty of purchasing and reviewing them. Now, Kaiming Bookstore has seen the need and reprinted the Twenty-Five Histories, reduced into nine volumes, and charged a low price, which is really immeasurable in helping the exploration and research of national history. It is hoped that schools, societies, and families will each have one copy, so that whether it is young students or social elders, or even housewives, can seek the process of the development of our Chinese nation in this, and even if they do not want to spontaneously generate a patriotic heart, they will not be able to. Therefore, Kaiming's reprinting of the Twenty-Five Histories is not only a blessing to the education sector, but also a small supplement to the future of the country and the nation. Reading its publication origin, I am happy to write this to promote it.

On the New History of Yuan and New Compilation of History of Yuan 224

— Lü Simian

Your letter suspects which of the books of Wei and Ke is applicable, and this is not doubtful. The official history is no longer entirely for the reading of ordinary people today, but specifically for the use of experts to extract materials. Those for ordinary people to read are troubled by its complexity, and those for experts to extract materials seek its completeness. Since the Tang Dynasty, the two have been impossible to combine. In ancient times, there were few historical materials, and historians' views were also rough, and the relationship between things was taken and discarded at will. Therefore, the resulting books cannot be very complex. After a dynasty is founded, the history of the previous dynasty can be read by ordinary people. The situation in later generations is different, and historical materials are always suffering from being too many. It is unbearable to abandon them during compilation, and it is too complicated to store them all. Those who discuss historical selection argue over the complexity and simplicity, and there is no plan, which is due to this (those who discuss may not know it themselves, but it is actually forced by this situation). At this time, books that preserve materials and books that are for ordinary people to read should be separated into two things. However, this principle did not become clear until Zhang Shizhai came out. Before this, historians mostly wandered between the two, which is why it was so difficult for them to write. However, rather than abandoning it, it is better to save it, everyone has this idea, which is why the official history is not expected to be complex and is becoming more and more complex. Then, the reason why later experts in history can draw on it is that they are given this gradual complexity. The strength of Ke's book lies in its completeness. The rewriting of the History of Yuan has been done for a long time. There are also many people who have revised and supplemented it. The books used are more or less, and the theories are right or wrong. To study this history today, one is not only troubled by the desolation of the old history, but also by the fact that there are too many materials outside the history that are not easy to collect, and there are many conflicting theories outside the history that are difficult to choose. Ke's book is diligent in collecting and cautious in compromising. With this, what the old history has left out and what later generations have revised and supplemented are all included in the two hundred and dozens of volumes, which is why it seems complex but is actually simple. Although Wei's book has a new style, it is too simple in its content. Moreover, they are all old theories from a hundred years ago. Not only have they not borrowed from Western history since Hong Wenqing, but also the historical materials stored in the country are not fully collected. Abandoning Ke's book and reading Wei's book, how can the other books not be covered? Then seeking simplicity becomes complexity. I was able to read Ke's book when it was first published, and I borrowed it from my predecessor, Mr. Tu Jingshan. After browsing through it, the teacher asked me: "What do you think?" I did not dare to answer and asked the teacher instead. The teacher said: "The strength of this book lies in its extensive collection, which can save those who study this history a lot of energy." I was very happy that his views were the same. The teacher also asked: "Since Ke's book has been ordered by the government and listed in the school officials, then among the official histories, Tang, Five Dynasties, and Yuan, there are two parallel lists. The students' daily efforts may be difficult to supply. If there is something to be established, can something be replaced?" I replied: "There are actually more overlapping official histories than this number. The differences and similarities between the Records of the Historian and the History of Han are mostly in wording, as are the books of Qi, Liang, Chen, Wei, Northern Qi, Zhou, and Sui in the History of the North and South. Moreover, there are those who originally had this defect and supplemented it with that one. But if there is a good collator who bases it on one and notes the differences and similarities of the other below, then one can be saved. There are too many differences and similarities between the New and Old Tang and Five Dynasties, even those that are the same are very different in wording, so they should be kept together. If the Old History of Yuan, then what it has is almost nothing beyond the New History. If you get its new, the old can almost be abandoned." The teacher also thought it was right. This matter has been more than ten years, and the teacher has also returned to the mountains for a long time, so I describe it sadly.

The Inspiration for a Comprehensive History of China 225

— Gu Xin’gang

The Twenty-Four Histories are difficult to acquire, even with modest means. The lithographic edition from the Tongwen Publishing House is much cheaper than the palace edition, yet still costs over two hundred yuan. Now, the Commercial Press is collecting and printing ancient editions, but even with pre-orders, it costs three hundred yuan. Those who can read often lack the means to buy, while those with the means often buy them for display. The mismatch between need and supply seems like an inherent flaw, causing one to sigh in contemplation. Now, the Kaiming Bookstore is using zinc plates to print the Twenty-Five Histories, with small but clear characters, and includes reference bibliographies and name indexes. The number of volumes is increased, making searching more convenient, while the price is reduced even further, benefiting scholars immensely. If they could build upon this ambition and expand it, from the Book of Documents and Zuo Zhuan to the Donghua Records and Draft History of Qing, further breaking down the traditional concept of "official history," categorizing works like the Sixteen Kingdoms Spring and Autumn Annals and the Ten Kingdoms Spring and Autumn Annals (historically called "unofficial histories") as "supplementary histories," and works like the Khitan National History and Great Jin National History as "separate histories," and compiling chronicles and essential records into one collection called "One Hundred Histories of China," their contribution to the academic world would be tenfold greater. In recent years, spurred by the times, the Chinese people are thinking about establishing a foundation for nationalism, and are eager to find a comprehensive history of China to read, but are hampered by the lack of such a book. This is due to a lack of individual talent and the inability to centralize materials. The Kaiming Bookstore colleagues are determined to promote culture, and it is hoped that they will seize this opportunity, take the lead, and work hard to collect historical books and compile indexes. As for analyzing materials, categorizing them, and verifying differences to achieve uniformity, this is our responsibility. In ten years, this will surely satisfy the nation's expectations.

Editor's Note: Mr. Gu expects us to take on the responsibility of broadly collecting historical materials and expanding from the "Twenty-Five Histories" to create a comprehensive "One Hundred Histories of China," which is a great honor! We are certainly happy to accept Mr. Gu's expectations. However, regarding broadly collecting historical materials and starting with the compilation and printing of the "Twenty-Five Histories," there are doubts and inquiries from outside, which need to be clarified. Our country has a vast amount of literature, and almost all books, in a broad sense, are historical materials. Even within the four categories of books, the history section alone has numerous classifications, too many to list. If we were to edit this vast historical literature, we could not do so without standards or haphazardly. However, everyone has their own subjective views, making it difficult to determine the standards. Before a standard is agreed upon, the official "standard histories" of the past can serve as temporary standards. If "standard histories" serve as temporary standards, then our preliminary work today is only to compile and print the "Twenty-Five Histories." If we were to print only the Twenty-Four Histories now and omit the "New History of Yuan," we would not only violate the temporary standard, but also feel outdated. If we do not attend to Mr. Gu's instructions for meaningful and systematic classification and broad compilation, then even two hundred and fifty histories or two hundred and sixty histories can be haphazardly gathered, but what would that achieve? Therefore, strictly speaking, the initial collection for compiling and printing historical books today should only consist of the "Twenty-Five Histories," and the number should not be arbitrarily reduced or expanded. Any expansion must be done in a meaningful and systematic way as instructed by Mr. Gu. This note is specially appended to express Mr. Gu's great kindness and to explain our work to those who care about it.

A New Path for Publishing Important Books 226

— Zhu Qifeng

The Kaiming Bookstore is taking the palace edition of the Twenty-Four Histories and combining it with Ke Shaomin's New History of Yuan, published by the Tuigengtang Publishing House, to create the Twenty-Five Histories, reducing them using zinc plates, and publishing them for the world. They asked me to say a few words as an introduction. The name "official history" originated in the History of the Sui Dynasty. The Song Dynasty designated Seventeen Histories, and subsequent additions led to the Qing Dynasty combining the Old Book of Tang and the Old History of the Five Dynasties into the Twenty-Four Histories. Since the Book of the Later Han, they have all followed the model of Ban Gu and Ban Zhao, with successive dynasties continuing the work, differing from the divergent and branching unofficial histories. There are many historical works, and without distinguishing them, they would become limitless. Therefore, the compilation of the Twenty-Four Histories, although originating from the so-called "imperial decree," has been undisputed by scholars to this day. The History of Yuan compiled during the Ming Dynasty had significant omissions. Ke Shaomin's New History of Yuan corrects errors and fills gaps, making significant contributions. Following the precedent of the New Book of Tang and the New History of the Five Dynasties, it is included in the official history, which can be said to be a proper and justified action. Before this, the official histories of previous dynasties were not complete without the Twenty-Four Histories, and now they cannot encompass the entirety of official history without the Twenty-Five Histories. Therefore, the name Twenty-Five Histories can be displayed proudly.

Furthermore, since the method of movable type printing has become popular, the publication of books has increased and accelerated. However, due to publishers seeking profit, they only aim for quick results, disregarding errors and omissions. I once exchanged several silver dollars for various typeset notebooks, and their value was only one-tenth of the price. Compared to fine woodblock-printed editions, they were less than one-hundredth as valuable. However, upon reading, numerous errors were found, making them unreadable. This made me think that if unscrupulous people were to hastily typeset and print important books from various categories and lower their prices to attract customers, then the disaster that befell the pear wood blocks in the past would now spread to the scholarly community. It is important to know that inaccurate proofreading of books can lead to errors that are insignificant at first but become serious mistakes later on. Lu Fangweng said that erroneous books scattered throughout the world mislead scholars even more, and it would be better not to publish them at all, expressing his deep concern. Every time I hear about the Commercial Press and the Zhonghua Book Company using photolithography to reprint old books, I rejoice and praise them. Fine editions are hard to come by, and proofreading is difficult. Now, with the help of cameras, the labor of typesetting and proofreading is saved, and there are no errors. It is truly a single action that achieves multiple benefits. The Kaiming Bookstore uses zinc plate reduction printing for the Twenty-Five Histories. Although the font is slightly smaller, it is clearer than lithographic printing. I once read the sample, and even with my old and blurry eyes, I could still recognize each character. The volume is smaller, and the price is lower. If they continue to take the essential books from the Siku Quanshu and make plates for reduction printing, then aspiring scholars, even if they are not from famous and wealthy families, can have ten thousand volumes at home. Wouldn't that be wonderful?

The Most Complete Collection of Standard Histories 227

— Zhang Shilu

The Kaiming edition of the Twenty-Five Histories is the newest and most complete collection of standard histories of past dynasties in our country. This book encompasses the main traces of various activities of the Chinese nation in the past. In the reading community, it is like cloth, beans, and millet, an indispensable classic, which needs no further discussion. What should be discussed is the current general attitude of the reading community towards classics. I fear they no longer have the leisurely time to read through the entire book, volume by volume, line by line, sentence by sentence, word by word. They only place it on their desks for occasional browsing and checking. Therefore, the classics published now must be comprehensive and also convenient for readers to carry, browse, and check. The Kaiming edition of the Twenty-Five Histories adds the New History of Yuan to the palace edition of the Twenty-Four Histories. The History of Ming also includes textual research. The end of the book also includes a name index, and each history also includes a list of references. In addition to convenient browsing, it can also inspire the minds of readers and researchers. It is comprehensive, and the space occupied by the entire book is minimal. Although the volume is small, the font is still very clear. Although the casting work is huge, the price is still very low. It strives to meet the needs of the general reading community today. I believe that this book is not only a treasure for historians but also a tool for promoting the culture of our nation. May the people of our country appreciate it!

Modern Printing Technology 228

— Editor

丨Photographic Zinc Plate Printing of the Twenty-Five Histories丨

Most people only know that there are two types of new printing methods: "letterpress printing" and "lithographic printing." This is not surprising because most popular books and newspapers are printed using these two methods. Even the storefronts of printing shops often display signs that say "Letterpress and Lithographic Printing." However, in more specialized terms, modern printing techniques should be divided into three types: first, relief printing; second, intaglio printing; and third, planographic printing. Relief printing uses the raised surface of the plate for printing. Traditional Chinese woodblock printing and modern letterpress printing both belong to this category. In contrast, intaglio printing uses the recessed surface, and the most common examples are banknotes and stamps. As for lithographic printing, it uses chemical reactions to display the text and images on a special lithographic stone. During printing, only the necessary parts can receive ink and be printed on paper, while the other parts are made ink-resistant. The plate is completely flat, with no raised or recessed areas, which is completely different from the previous two types, so it belongs to planographic printing. Among these three types of printing, intaglio printing is not commonly used for printing books because the plate making and printing are very troublesome, and it is only suitable for printing fine items. Therefore, the common printing of books only uses relief and planographic printing.

However, relief printing is not limited to letterpress printing, and planographic printing is not limited to lithographic printing. Similar to lithographic printing, there are metal plates—zinc plates, aluminum plates (commonly known as lead skin plates), and offset plates (commonly known as rubber plates). In addition to letterpress printing, relief printing also includes photographic zinc plates, photographic halftone copper plates, and electroplated copper plates. The current Kaiming edition of the Twenty-Five Histories is printed using photographic zinc plates. This printing method is exactly the same as letterpress printing on the printing press. In other words, it uses the same letterpress printing machine, not a lithographic printing machine. However, letterpress printing combines individual movable types after proofreading, while zinc plate printing uses photographic methods to create a negative image of the original manuscript, which is transferred to a zinc plate coated with a photosensitive agent. Light is used to make the zinc plate display text that is the opposite of the original manuscript. Then, the photosensitive agent in the non-photosensitive areas is washed away, leaving only the photosensitive areas. Special chemicals are then used to make these areas acid-resistant, and finally, an acidic agent is used to corrode the other areas, leaving only the acid-resistant areas. The zinc plate produced in this way is almost the same as a letterpress plate composed of movable types, except that the zinc plate is a bit harder than the letterpress plate.

Since it is also relief printing, why not use letterpress printing but use photographic zinc plate printing for the Twenty-Five Histories? This question can be answered in a simple sentence: For a large book with four or five million words, it is impossible to proofread it without errors in a short period of time and with a small number of people. Only a precise camera can be used as a copying writer to reproduce it on the zinc plate. It can be responsible for being absolutely error-free, although the salary of this copying writer may be higher than that of the "humble people" and proofreaders combined.

However, planographic printing can also use photography. Why abandon planographic printing and use relief printing? It is true that photographic lithography is used a lot in popular books on the market, and even metal plates or rubber plates are often used to reproduce ancient books from the Song and Yuan dynasties. But if you compare a letterpress-printed book with a lithographic-printed book, you can see the differences. If you have ever seen fine-print lithographic books such as the Romance of the Three Kingdoms and Water Margin printed on glossy paper, you must have felt disgusted by the blurry fonts and floating ink. Of course, inferior letterpress-printed books often have the problem of being like a layer of clouds due to the corrosion of the lead types and the impurity of the ink, but they still feel more real than those lithographic-printed books. This is because lithographic printing uses a planographic plate, and the inked and non-inked parts on the planographic plate are at the same level. Although machine pressure is applied during printing, the paper is not as likely to be closely attached to the plate surface as in relief printing, especially with relatively rough or hard paper. Moreover, in planographic printing, the entire plate surface is rolled over by the ink roller. Although the non-inked parts are wiped with water, there are always some residual areas. The fine black dots in lithographic-printed books are due to this reason. As for photographic stone printing, the stone surface often cannot be as clear as the photograph, so it must be manually retouched. Sometimes, due to unclear fonts, workers make mistakes when writing from memory, which is also common. These common problems in lithographic printing can be reduced a lot in the more advanced lead skin plates or rubber plates, but they are not as good as photographic zinc plates printed using relief printing. Especially since the Twenty-Five Histories uses relatively rough newsprint to reduce costs, and the fonts are relatively small, planographic printing is not as clear as relief printing, which is the biggest reason for using relief printing.

Printing is an industrial technology, and most readers may not pay much attention to these relatively specialized trivial matters. However, publishers should carefully consider them. This is just to express our considerations so that everyone can understand.

Education News

Ministry of Education Orders That Salaries of Military Instructors in High Schools Be Paid as Usual 232

(Nanjing, 20th) The Ministry of Education compiled a book of education laws and regulations from March of last year to June of the third year and issued a notice to all departments and bureaus on the 20th. The Ministry of Education approved a report from the General Directorate of Training, stating that when schools end the military training for second-year students according to the transitional measures, the treatment of military instructors should remain at the original level. It has now issued a notice to all departments and bureaus stating that military instructors in schools should be full-time in principle, and the treatment of military instructors has been revised. Article 6 of the military education plan for high schools and above clearly stipulates that after the military training for second-year students in senior high schools and equivalent schools is completed, the number of hours taught by military instructors will inevitably decrease. The schools should still maintain the original amount of salary paid to the military instructors according to the plan and should not reduce it on the pretext of decreasing hours taught. The order is hereby issued for compliance.

Ministry of Education Will Strictly Prohibit Correspondence Courses in Medicine 233

The Ministry of Interior believes that medical education is related to people's lives, and not only emphasizes the exploration of academic theory, but also emphasizes experience and practice. It has recently found that medical correspondence schools in various provinces and cities are enrolling students. This situation will inevitably cause many errors in the future. It has specially requested the Ministry of Education to instruct the education departments and bureaus of various provinces and cities to strictly prohibit correspondence courses in medicine. After approving the report, the Ministry of Education will issue a notice to the education departments and bureaus of various provinces and cities to investigate and prohibit them separately.

The Ministry of Education will hold the inaugural meeting of the National Council of the China Boy Scout General Association on the 19th, take over the preparatory office at the end of October, and start working on November 1st. The General Association is considered to be established. The organization consists of Jiang Zhongzheng as the president, Dai Chuanxian as the vice president, followed by directors (such as the 15 directors mentioned in the newspaper), secretaries, etc. It is reported that the work plan for this year after the establishment of the association includes drafting various regulations and detailed rules for the association, "Election Rules for Councils at All Levels," "Various Regulations for Boy Scout Service Personnel," "Detailed Course Outlines for Boy Scouts at All Levels," "Editing Boy Scout Monthly and Reference Books," "Continuing to Handle the Registration of Boy Scouts and Service Personnel Nationwide," "Preparing for the National Boy Scout Jamboree and Grand Review," and "Other Important Regulations Related to Boy Scouts," etc. It is also reported that the association plans to build a new clubhouse through fundraising.

Opening of the City's Elementary School Holiday Homework Exhibition Yesterday 237

Director Pan Presided and Delivered a Speech on Behalf of the Mayor

25,000 Exhibits Displayed in 14 Rooms

The Exhibition Continues This Morning and Closes at Noon

Exhibits from Each School Must Be Retrieved from 1 PM

The first city-wide elementary school holiday homework exhibition, organized by the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education and the Children's Morning Post, opened at 9:00 AM yesterday at Wanzhu Elementary School. The exhibition continues this morning for half a day, and exhibits will be collected by each school from 1:00 PM to 2:00 PM this afternoon. Details are as follows:

A Glimpse of the Venue The entrance to the exhibition is at the main entrance of Wanzhu Elementary School on Luxiangyuan Road. A huge bamboo cloth banner hangs in front of the gate. There is a signing area at the entrance. A couplet hangs in front of the stage in the main auditorium: "Remarkable Achievements Obtained During the Holidays," "Diligent Homework with Careful Observation." The exhibition rooms are located upstairs and downstairs in the central and northern buildings. Boy Scouts provide service along the way, and the organizing committee sends personnel to serve as receptionists and marshals. This time, 57 schools participated with more than 25,000 exhibits, displayed in 14 rooms. The exhibits, all created by students in the third grade and above during the summer vacation, such as various plant specimens and artistic works, are quite excellent.

Opening Ceremony The opening ceremony was held at 9:00 AM. Present were Pan Gongzhan, Director of the Municipal Bureau of Education; Wang Longzhang, representative of the Municipal Party Headquarters; Yan Wenkai, representative of the Social Affairs Bureau; and Zhou You, Hu Shuyi, Zhang Yongshou, Qian Fugong, Zhao Zengqi, guest Jiang Xicen, and more than 500 teachers and students from various schools. Director Pan served as chairman, Sun Yucai and Lü Xinfu as recorders, and Wu Renya as master of ceremonies. The ceremony proceeded as scheduled. First, the chairman reported, followed by Director Pan delivering a speech on behalf of Mayor Wu, and Wang Longzhang, representative of the Municipal Party Headquarters, delivered a speech. Guest Jiang Xicen gave a speech. The ceremony concluded at around 11:00 AM.

Chairman's Report Chairman Pan reported that the exhibition was originally scheduled to close on the 1st, but due to the large number of visitors, it was decided to extend it for half a day and close it at 12:00 noon on Sunday. A total of 57 elementary schools participated this time, with more than 25,400 exhibits. The exhibition is jointly organized by the Municipal Bureau of Education and the Children's Morning Post. The purpose is to encourage students to do homework during the holidays so that they understand that they should also study on their own during the holidays. This session is experimental in nature. Because the announcement was too late, schools had already started their summer vacation, so most of them did not have time to prepare and participate. Next year, the regulations will be announced earlier, and the Children's Morning Post will publish the topics and materials in each issue, and students will create their own during the holidays. After the start of school, they will be submitted to the schools, and the teachers will hold internal exhibitions, select exhibits, and then hold a city-wide exhibition. However, I would like to report to you that the purpose of holding this exhibition is to enable students to be automatic, self-study, self-made, and self-controlled. It is not allowed for schools to forge them. Now, perhaps many schools have the wrong idea that the grades are related to the school's reputation, and others make them on their behalf, pretending to be student works. This should be prohibited. First, we must make students break the concept of not working for gain. Second, the achievements of this exhibition will be used as the standard for next year, and we must make progress every year, which is a good achievement for the school. I hope that all schools will guide students not to waste their time during the summer vacation.

Mayor's Speech Director Pan delivered a speech on behalf of Mayor Wu, stating that the mayor could not attend today because he was attending the air defense coordination meeting. The mayor's intention is to make elementary school students understand the danger of the country and the importance of future responsibilities. Saving the country depends entirely on young people. The more dangerous the country, the greater the responsibility of young people. In the past, King Goujian of Yue endured hardship and made great efforts, and after ten years of recovery and ten years of training, he was finally able to destroy Wu and avenge his past shame. The so-called ten years of recovery and ten years of training is to tell everyone that the elderly and middle-aged people have no hope. Ten years of recovery and ten years of training is to cultivate new people. From childhood to ten years old, the body must be well nourished, and there must be many. After ten years old, add another ten years of strict training, and only at twenty years old can they become strong men who can defeat the Wu Kingdom. China must also teach and nurture children well. I hope that all of you children will work hard.

Start Judging The judging began yesterday afternoon. The judging committee members were Ni Wenya, Chen Xuanhan, Jiang Xicen, Dong Renjian, Zong Lianghuan, Zeng Shengdian, Ge Liting, Han Mingyi, Xu Yingchang, Hu Zuyin, Zeng Zhenqing, Zhou Peicheng, Huang Juemin, Zhang Zubei, and Shu Xincheng, etc. The exhibits from each school are divided into two types: competition and free participation, and judged by subject. Because the units are individuals and schools, the judging procedures are quite troublesome. Last night, the Municipal Bureau of Education invited the committee members to dine at the YMCA.

Health Guidance Health guidance and hygiene affairs are handled by Dr. Zhang Qi and nurse Jiang Yifan from the Health Bureau, who set up a separate hygiene room to handle hygiene business and provide family health guidance. If parents have any health or disease problems, they can go to ask.

Extended for Half a Day The exhibition was originally scheduled for one day. However, because the crowds of visitors yesterday blocked the roads, it was decided to extend it for half a day. It will close at 12:00 noon today. Before 12:00 noon, it will still be open to the public. The association welcomes parents to visit to build a foundation for communication between family and school and to promote the progress of students' physical, mental, and academic development. The time for each school to collect exhibits is from 1:00 PM to 2:00 PM this afternoon.

Commercial Press Holds Intelligence Competition for Young Children 245

Held for Nine Days from October 20th to 28th

Top 20 Receive Prizes of 5 to 20 Yuan Each

The Commercial Press on Henan Road in this city initiated and held a physical fitness competition for children on Children's Day this year, which has won a lot of praise from the society. It is generally believed that it has great significance for children's education. In order to test children's intelligence, the library will hold an intelligence competition for young children in the library from the 20th to the 28th of this month, so that children's mental development and physical fitness can be properly developed at the same time. The first test and testers were all students of Junde Elementary School yesterday. The testing method is to print various pictures and ask children to use a red pencil to circle within five seconds, such as what is used for eating, what can fly, what is used together, what picture is painted well, etc. After the test, each child is given a picture book. After the competition is over, the results will be evaluated and prizes will be awarded. The top 20 will receive book coupons worth 5 to 20 yuan each. The original letter to the principals of various elementary schools is recorded as follows: Principal, we held a children's physical fitness competition on Children's Day this year, which was praised by educators and believed to have great significance for children's education. Our hopes for children are the same as your expectations for students, that is, we hope that children's mental development and physical fitness can be properly developed at the same time. Therefore, we are holding the "Intelligence Competition for Young Children" again. Because of the testing materials, the age must be slightly limited. The method is as follows: Location: The publishing office of the library on Henan Road. "Date" From October 20th to October 28th, Monday to Saturday from 9:30 AM to 5:30 PM, Sunday from 1:00 PM to 5:30 PM "Intelligence Test" The test is designed by experts and Mr. Tai Shuangqiu, Dean of the College of Education of Daxia University, and Mr. Dong Renjin, Director of the Chinese Children's Education Society, are invited as consultants. All materials are full of interest, and all methods and calculations of results are very scientific, so children of all ages within the age limit can be compared. "Age Limit" From 5 to 8 years old "Gifts" Every child who participates in the competition will receive a small gift. "Prizes" The top 20 will receive book coupons worth 5 to 20 yuan each. If the principal or grade teacher of your school leads all or several teams of students in the first and second grades of your school or kindergarten to our institute for group testing, it will be especially welcome. Our institute also has the following requests and explanations: (1) Please take care of the students on the way to and from school to ensure safety. (2) It is best to come between 9:30 AM and 12:00 PM, as there are more people participating in the afternoon and on Sundays, and you may have to wait a long time, or please write a letter in advance to arrange a date and time. (3) The participating children must be within the above age and be able to understand Mandarin or Shanghainese. The number of people tested each time is about 30 to 40. (4) Participation in the test requires an admission ticket, one for each person. Please fill in each item in detail in advance and bring it with you. Twenty copies are attached for your use. If it is not enough, please inform us by letter or fill it out when you come to our institute. Special letter invitation, looking forward to your visit, Shanghai Publishing Office of Commercial Press.

Sports News

Little Hero Raises Eyebrows and Exceeds Expectations Zheng Zhaojia Defeats Carlson 249

Overcomes the Shanghai Singles Champion 3-1

Wins the China Tennis Club Group A Championship

The result of the China Tennis Club Group A singles final yesterday was beyond expectations. The audience raised their eyebrows and rejoiced. Zheng Zhaojia lived up to expectations and defeated the Shanghai singles champion Carlson 3-1 to win the championship, regaining a lot of honor for Chinese tennis players. His skillful hitting is especially commendable. The results are as follows:

Zheng Zhaojia (6-4 3-6 6-2 6-3) Carlson

Hitting the Nail on the Head 250

The appropriate hitting and strategy were the main reasons for Zheng's victory over Carlson yesterday. Knowing yourself and knowing your enemy, you will win every battle. Zheng was able to attack Carlson's weaknesses, so he won. The cross-court rallies on both sides made Carl tired of running, and when Carl went to the net to intercept, Zheng was able to hit Carl's backhand with a cross-court shot, making Carl helpless. Standing in front of the net like a wooden chicken, therefore, he did not easily go to the net. Zheng did not use many lobs, so Carlson's smash could hardly be used. It is a pity that Zheng's smash is still weak and the action is still slow, otherwise controlling Carlson would be a matter of course.

Exhausted and Defeated 251

Carlson was still trying to make a final struggle in the fourth set at 5-4, but he was exhausted and had to admit defeat. Carlson's performance yesterday, except for being able to run and move faster than Zheng, was far from satisfactory. Zheng's body yesterday was at its best. In contrast, Carlson was exhausted and tired, so even if he fought to the fifth set, there was no doubt that Zheng would win. Carlson had few chances to smash yesterday, and his serve was also wrong and weak. He was repeatedly defeated by Zheng in front of the net, and he was tired of dealing with long rallies, and he was listless, so how could he not be defeated?

Taking the Lead 252

Except for the second set won by Carl, Zheng had an absolute advantage in the other three sets. 6-4 from 4-2 in the first set, 6-2 from 2-1 in the third set, and 6-4 from 5-2 from 3-1 in the fourth set. Even in the second set, which was won by Carlson, Zheng once led 3-1. Carlson won five consecutive games to win 6-3. Therefore, Zheng's victory yesterday was very easy. Carlson served first, and Zheng scored, so each scored one point each, and Zheng took a 4-2 lead with cross-court rallies on both sides. But Carl served and also won two consecutive games, making it 4-4. However, Carl's serve failed in the next game, and Zheng served. Carl touched the net three times in a row, and Zheng won the first set 6-4.

Continuing Efforts 253

Carl still served first in the second set. Carl began to go to the net to intercept, but Zheng attacked Carl's backhand with a very skillful backhand cross-court shot, making Carl unable to return the ball. Zheng then won two consecutive games, leading 3-1. At this time, Zheng gradually saw many balls going out of bounds and not passing the net. Carlson took the opportunity to advance and won five consecutive games, winning the second set 6-3. At the beginning of the third set, Carl won two more games. Zheng was greatly encouraged and won six consecutive games in one breath, winning 6-2. Therefore, Zheng took the lead again with two to one.

Final Battle 254

Carlson lost six consecutive games and lost the third set, and his physical exhaustion was obvious. During the rest period, the two regained their spirits, especially Zheng Zhaojia, who was not tired at all. Zheng served first and won, taking a 1-0 lead. Unfortunately, Zheng's serve failed in the next game. Fortunately, Carl's situation was not good, and he wanted to make a final bet, chasing it to 5-3. Zheng served and took a 40-30 lead, but Carl won and made it 5-4. At this time, the tension in the air was unparalleled. Because Carl served in the next game, it would become 5-5, and the future victory or defeat would be unpredictable. Zheng pulled it back from 30-40 to equality, passing through twelve equalizations, one after another, Carlson was exhausted and defeated, and the final set was 6-4.

Seventh Annual West China Basketball Tournament Registration Begins Today 257

Deadline: November 1st

Tournament Starts: November 19th

The seventh annual West China Basketball Championship is scheduled to open on November 19th. Invitations have been sent out by West China. This year, in addition to the A and B groups, a C group will be added. The details of the three groups are as follows:

Group A: Group A will accommodate twelve teams, three Western teams, seven Chinese university teams, and the remaining two teams will be selected from independent team applications. If there are many applicants, a double-elimination method will be used.

Group B: Group B is divided into two subgroups, each with seven teams. Western and Chinese applicants will be accepted. However, if the total number exceeds fourteen teams, the weaker Chinese teams will be eliminated using a double-elimination method to reach the number of fourteen teams.

Group C: The newly established Group C will have a maximum of eight teams. This group is for middle school teams. University and Western teams that meet the middle school skill level will be combined into this group. This year, West China will have four teams participating: two in Group A, one in Group B, and one in Group C.

Time: All groups will adopt a single round-robin system. Each half of Group A games will be twenty minutes, and each half of Groups B and C will be fifteen minutes. Approximately nineteen matches will be played each week, from 7:15 PM to 9:30 PM. On Saturdays, games will start from 4:00 PM.

Registration: Registration begins today and ends on November 1st. Elimination matches are scheduled to begin on November 12th, and the official competition will begin on November 19th and end in mid-January.

Women's: The women's competition this year will be held after the men's competition, approximately in mid-January. West China has been in contact with Hai Qing, and West China will continue to hold the competition after the Hai Qing Championship ends.

Meiyuan Gymnasium to be Completed Soon 259

Maple Floor Suitable for Skating, Tennis, and Basketball

Divided into Six Major Sections, Qiu Feihai Invited to Collaborate

The sports community of this city, in order to promote sports and provide a place for all sectors to exercise and strengthen their bodies, previously raised funds to build the large-scale Meiyuan Gymnasium on Route Ghisi, and invited Qiu Feihai and others to cooperate. Construction began some time ago and is expected to be completed by mid-next month. The details are reported as follows:

Occupying Seven Mu with Excellent Facilities: The initiators believe that Shanghai is densely populated, but the facilities for sports are scarce. In order to make a significant contribution to the practice of both Chinese and foreigners, they raised 120,000 yuan to lease seven and a half mu of land on Route Ghisi in the French Concession to build the Meiyuan Gymnasium. The floor is made of the most durable maple wood. This wood can be used as a skating rink and as a hard tennis court, which is very convenient.

Completion Next Month, Divided into Six Sections: This building was designed by Sandbrook & Co. and constructed by Wu Cangji Construction Company. Since the start of construction, most of it has been completed and is scheduled to open around the 20th of next month. The construction capital is a Sino-Western joint venture. The main initiator, Mr. Scott, also invited tennis master Qiu Feihai to cooperate. Qiu believes that tennis is usually stopped in winter due to weather conditions. Now that there are indoor facilities, there are more opportunities for practice and no conflict of schedules. He expressed his approval. It is reported that the museum is divided into skating, tennis, boxing, fitness, basketball, and wine and card games.

The Gold Market Still Shows a Strong Upward Trend

Resulting in a Rebound of Thirteen Yuan

The gold market is showing a strong upward trend. Although there was a reaction the day before yesterday, the market rebounded again yesterday. Even with the establishment of the 100 million yuan stabilization fund, the upward sentiment is still difficult to suppress. As a result, the market opened slightly weak yesterday, but ended with a rebound. In the early morning, the foreign silver increased and the British rose, and the U.S. dollar remained flat, and the exchange rate increased slightly, but it was irrelevant. The price of London gold fell by five pence, and it was predicted that the Customs Gold (關金) listing would shrink, so the market opened outside the venue and was slightly weak, retreating to 834 yuan. The report that the stabilization fund jointly formed by the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications decided to first use 100 million yuan to suppress the local exchange rate market caused a slight impact on people's hearts, and the selling side turned enthusiastic and broke the 80 yuan mark. After the opening, the market hovered around 80 yuan. Grain and Flour Market Morning Fall, Afternoon Rise 279

The flour market opened with a small drop of 2-3 fen, due to the tired trend of the previous day, there were sales of both long and short positions, factories sold far-month contracts, and customers bought near-term contracts, so there was this small state. Then, the low price caused large off-market players to hoard and sell, and factories did not sell much in the far term, and supplementing near-term contracts was healthier, so the market turned sharply upward. In the afternoon, with the soaring price of gold, people's minds and the market both rebounded upward, and the far month was competed for by all parties, and the rise was even faster. The closing price of the current month rose by 3 fen and 25/100, the next month rose by 4 fen and 75/100, December rose by 5 fen and a half, January rose by 6 fen and 75/100, and February also rose by 6 fen and 75/100, etc.

After the wheat market opened in the morning, the various months continued the downward trend of the previous day, and many long positions were nervously closed out, and new shorts were also sold, and the opening price immediately dropped by 6-7-8 fen. Then, due to the rise in gold prices and the sharp rise in flour prices, selling was stopped, and new hoarding and short covering became active, and the market rose step by step. The market atmosphere was even better in the afternoon, and the closing price of the current month rose by 8 fen, November and February rose by 4 fen, December rose by 7 fen, and January rose by 3 fen. Currently, the foreign market is weak, and market prices are unlikely to rise greatly. Wheat opened with heavy selling, and market prices fell, but quickly rebounded. Public opinion believes that the market will not fall sharply. If the foreign side can provide considerable stimulus, the market will be high, because the domestic situation is very good.

Spring and Autumn Children's Weekly

Toy Imports and Homemade Toys 286

— Jin Xi

Generally speaking, toys are our children's second life. Toys can develop our emotions, senses, knowledge, and will.

However, from another perspective, according to a survey by the International Trade Bureau, the total number of foreign games and toys imported in the past eight months amounted to over 664,000 national currency, an increase of one-fifth compared to last year (last year's total was over 580,000). Among them, Japanese toy imports were the most numerous. Therefore, our children have developed a contradictory mentality. We cannot do without toys, but the drain on resources from toys is such an alarming figure. Facts do not allow us to need toys anymore. If we want toys again, we are not patriotic; if we love the country, we can no longer have toys.

In fact, we don't need to worry so much. In the future, we have two ways to remedy the drain on resources from toys: (1) Make our own toys. We follow the toy-making methods in books and make them ourselves, and ask the craft teachers in the school to guide us. (2) Buy domestic toys. If the structure of the toy is too complicated for us to make, then we will buy domestic toys and ask our parents to carefully identify the trademarks.

Great People All Have a Love of Reading 287

— Da Zhai

The current British Prime Minister, MacDonald, is one who likes to read most. He is often reading, and reading hardly ever stops. When he deals with official business, he continuously reads the government documents page by page for several hours, and only stops when he has finished reading. This shows that he reads in order, not flipping through randomly and without order. Children often have a bad habit of reading. When they get a book, they look at the back without looking at the front; or they abandon reading this book before finishing it to look at that one. When asked what the book is about, they still cannot answer. This is very bad. We should take MacDonald as an example to learn how to read, so that we can comprehend the meaning. Reading is his lifelong habit. He liked to read, observe, and study all kinds of problems when he was a child. He often said to people, "The reason why he was able to develop to a new position was because of reading."

Mr. Sun Yat-sen said, "In my life, apart from revolution, reading is my only hobby. I cannot live without reading for a day." He carried books with him even when supervising battles on the front lines, and his usual love of reading can be imagined. Therefore, he was able to write many books on academic theory.

When Zeng Wenzhenggong led troops, he had a set time for reading and writing every day as a routine task, which was never interrupted. Once, an epidemic spread among the troops, causing successive deaths, and they were surrounded by enemy troops. However, he remained undisturbed and recited as usual. With such a calm and focused spirit, he was not only good at martial arts but also good at literature.

Children, if you also want to become great people and save the country from difficulties, you must love reading.

Mosquitoes 288

— Sheng Huai

Mosquitoes! Mosquitoes! Constantly buzzing by my pillow! I have no hatred or resentment towards you. Why do you disturb my sweet dreams?

Mosquitoes! Mosquitoes! I have already tolerated you for disturbing my sweet dreams. I have no hatred or resentment towards you. Why do you still prick my skin, suck my blood, and make me feel pain?

Hateful mosquitoes! Evil mosquitoes! My spirit has suffered your pain! My body has suffered your pain! Except for puppets, who would be tolerant! Raise my giant palm, pat! pat! pat! Please meet your end!

Mosquitoes! Mosquitoes! It's not that my heart is cruel, but your future troubles are truly endless!

Victory Belongs to the Brave 289

— Hui Xian

Children! You should remember this sentence well... Victory belongs to the brave!

The brave are forward-moving and fearless. They defeat all obstacles and enemies. Victory belongs to them! The timid shrink back and will never have a successful career!

If you don't believe me, please read the following story.

Before the Russo-Japanese War, a Russian officer and a Japanese officer were drinking together in a tavern in Vladivostok. They both got very drunk, and then they started talking more, each exaggerating the soldiers of their own country. The two had a big argument. Finally, they decided to have their guards compete on the flat rooftop of the tavern.

First, the Russian soldiers practiced. When the team gradually approached the edge of the roof, the soldiers' steps, without prior agreement, began to shrink. When they reached the edge of the roof, they stopped marching and did not move forward, even though the officer did not shout the commands to halt or march in place.

Later, it was the Japanese soldiers' turn to practice, and they did it in the same way as the Russian soldiers.

However, when the Japanese soldiers approached the edge of the roof, they did not flinch at all. They still marched forward with their heads held high. When they reached the edge, the officer did not shout the command to halt, and they rushed off the roof and fell straight down.

This is a demonstration of bravery.

Later, in the Russo-Japanese War, Japan ultimately defeated Russia.

Therefore, I say: Victory belongs to the bravest! Children, remember it well.

Why Can't People Live Long! 290

— Rong Yu

The length of an animal's life is directly proportional to the slowness of its growth. Those that grow quickly have short lives; those that grow slowly naturally have long lives. According to zoologists' estimates, the ratio between growth and age for ordinary animals is one to ten. For example, if a dog grows up in one year, it will live for ten years; if a cat grows up in six months, it will only have six years of survival. Animals like deer, cranes, and turtles grow very slowly, so their lives are also very long.

Humans grow up in sixteen years at the earliest and twenty years at the latest. According to the calculation, they should live to be one hundred and sixty to two hundred years old. Why don't we see people of such a great age? In reality, it is because humans are too intelligent. The rise and fall of the seven emotions and six desires has already discounted their age. The food they eat, cooked and fried, has so many varieties, which also makes the stomach and intestines prone to disease. In addition, as civilization evolves day by day, the body's original resistance also weakens day by day. Therefore, once attacked by disease, it is easy to die young. So the reason why people cannot live long is actually their own fault.

Ants with Social Organization 291

— Ruo Peng

I felt very bored at home and couldn't think of anything interesting to do as a pastime. After thinking for about half an hour, I came up with something that was very ordinary but very interesting.

I took a fly swatter and hit a fly. After looking at the ground for a long time, I found one or two ants. I dropped the dead fly next to the ants. Their antennae slightly touched it, and they tried to drag it with a little force, but it didn't move at all. Then, they climbed on the fly and kissed it with their sense of smell, and then ran down, shaking their heads, as if to call for reinforcements.

After a while, I saw a very orderly team of soldiers coming out of the cracks in the stone under the pillars, gradually approaching from a distance. Later, they actually reached their destination. Their order was very good. They worked together to drag the fly into the hole as if they were flying. However, there were still a few foraging ants running around outside.

After seeing this interesting thing, I felt that these very small animals were very good at maintaining order and neatness. Are we not as good as these small animals? Children! You should cultivate the spirit of ants. No matter when, you must have order and neatness. Then, when you go out into society, you will definitely be able to become good citizens!

Children's Science Lecture Series 293

— Lin Yin

The water vapor contained in the air will definitely condense when it encounters cold air, and this condensation is what forms clouds.

People who care about the weather must often look up at the clouds in the sky. Many clouds mean it will rain, few clouds mean the weather is very good, high clouds, low clouds, clouds moving south, clouds moving north, all can be observed from the clouds to see if the weather is good or bad. On the other hand, the shapes and colors of the clouds are very beautiful. When the sun rises or when the sun sets, the clouds at that time are so magical! Because of this, there are many kinds of clouds, distinctions, and names. It is necessary knowledge for children to study science!

Clouds can be roughly divided into ten types: (1) Stratus clouds, which are fog clouds, are the lowest type of cloud. On cloudy days, the ones covering the top of the hill are stratus clouds. (2) Nimbus clouds, also called chaotic clouds, are dark in color. When it rains, the black clouds stacked in layers are nimbus clouds. (3) Cumulus clouds are like overlapping white cotton, forming a round shape, and are most common in summer. (4) Thunderclouds, also known as cumulonimbus clouds, are a mixture of cumulus and nimbus clouds. The "cloud peaks" mentioned in books refer to this type of thundercloud. (5) Stratocumulus clouds are large, spiral-shaped, dark gray cloud masses. They look like it's going to rain, but they are not actually rain clouds. This type of cloud is most common in winter, blocking the sunlight and making the weather colder. (6) Cirrus clouds, also called streak clouds, are often seen in the blue sky as streaks like white brush bristles. If there is a slight breeze, it looks like smoke billowing from a flame. It is the highest type of cloud. Changes in the weather can be known by observing the direction of movement of this cloud. If it comes from the north, it means the weather is clear. If it comes from the south, the weather will be bad. (7) Cirrostratus clouds are formed by the accumulation of cirrus clouds covering the sky, like thin gauze. (8) Cirrocumulus clouds are small, white patches like fish scales, so they are also called scaly clouds. (9) Altocumulus clouds are similar to cirrocumulus clouds but larger, gray-white in color, and look like flocks of sheep in a pasture from a distance, so they are also called sheep clouds. (10) Altostratus clouds are gray and look like curtains stretched across the sky. They can often be seen before it rains, and are similar to nimbus clouds. Sometimes altostratus clouds can accumulate and form nimbus clouds.

Clouds are also related to cold climates. In the hot weather of summer, clouds can make it cooler. In the cold nights of winter, clouds can also make it warmer. Children may want to try it out.

Improved Windmill 294

— Yong Cai

Children! Don't you like windmills very much? Indeed, windmills are a refined and interesting toy. If we make a few more with colored paper and string them together, they will be especially fun when they dance in the wind! However, ordinary windmills (as shown in Figure 1) not only waste paper but are also too monotonous. Now we have an improved windmill that seems to save paper and is more beautiful than the ordinary one. I would like to offer it to the children. The following is its manufacturing method:

If you want to make an eight-corner windmill, first cut the scrap paper into eight identical 45-degree triangles (as shown in Figure 2), then cut a small round piece of paper and paste the corner A of the eight triangular papers onto the small drawing paper in sequence (as shown in Figure 3). After pasting them firmly, paste one corner of the eight pieces of paper onto another small round piece of paper in sequence (as shown in Figure 4). The front and back are the same as ordinary windmills. Drill two holes and it's done. Children! Do you see! Isn't this kind of windmill much more beautiful than the ordinary one? If you want to make it more complicated, you just need to add a few more triangular pieces of paper, and twelve-corner and sixteen-corner shapes can also be made in the same way.

Also, if you think the windmill doesn't turn smoothly, you just need to glue a small paper ring (about 1 fen long and 1 and a half fen in diameter) to the bamboo skewer on the back of the windmill, and it will turn even more smoothly.

Using windmills to measure wind direction is often very accurate. If you want to play, make four windmills of the same size, connect them in a cross shape on a bamboo pole, and insert it in the highest place in the courtyard, and you can observe the wind. However, there are two things to pay attention to: First, make sure to identify the correct direction. Second, make a special and clear mark representing the direction on each of the four windmills.

The Toad That Overestimated Itself 295

— Li Kui

There was a toad who lived with its children in a puddle.

One day, a cow came to the puddle to drink water, and the little toads cried out, "Look, how big the cow is!"

"Big!" their mother said disapprovingly, "What's wrong with you! I think it's only a little bigger than me. If I puff up my belly, I can catch up with it!"

So, it took a long breath and tried its best to puff up its belly.

"Look!" it asked, "Am I as big as the cow this time?"

"Oh! No!" the little toads answered in unison.

It puffed up its belly again with more force, and it looked like its belly was about to burst.

"Am I as big as the cow this time?" it asked.

"Oh, no!" the little toads answered in unison again.

However, the toad was very unconvinced. It refused to stop and continued to puff up its belly as before, until: Bang! It burst into pieces.

Model Children's Creed 296

— Yao Zhanwang

Loyalty: Treat people sincerely, without falsehood or deceit.

Frugality: Save money, be simple and unadorned.

Hard work: Work conscientiously, without complaining about hardship.

Kindness: Treat things with a calm and peaceful mind.

Respect: Follow the rules, be strict in speech and action.

Righteousness and courage: Suppress the strong and support the weak, care for the poor and help the needy.

Punctuality: Rest and work on time, without laziness or neglect.

Order: Practice the covenant, in an orderly manner.

Politeness: Respect teachers and love classmates.

Diligence: Strive in studies and work hard to explore.

Cleanliness: Clothes and utensils should be clean and tidy.

Agility: Thoughts and actions should be concise and decisive.

Caution in friendship: Be cautious and respectful in friendship, from beginning to end.

Public morality: Eliminate selfish thoughts, be selfless and impartial.

Love for the group: Be loving and sincere, use collective wisdom and strength.

Obedience: Abide by discipline and obey orders.

Progressiveness: Strive for self-improvement, be indomitable.

Self-reliance: Be independent and rely on no one.

Airplanes Are Lighter Than Feathers 297

— Ku

One day, when we were in common sense class, Mr. Hu asked everyone, "What is the lightest thing in the world?"

I stood up and answered, "Feathers are the lightest!"

Kong, who was sitting opposite me, hurriedly interrupted, "Airplanes are the lightest."

Mr. Hu asked him, "How do you know?"

Kong said, "Because I often see feathers flying in the air, and they fall down soon, and they don't fly high; but I often see airplanes flying to very high skies, and they still don't fall down, so they must be lighter than feathers!"
